I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
s2n-tls server reports signature scheme with RSA kex
### Security issue notifications

If you discover a potential security issue in s2n we ask that you notify
AWS Security via our [vulnerability reporting page](http://aws.amazon.com/security/vulnerability-reporting/). Please do **not** create a public github issue.

### Problem:

When a TLS handshake uses RSA kex, no separate signature is required. The server proves its ownership of the RSA certificate by encrypting/decrypting the premaster secret instead.

If you negotiate with RSA kex, you will see the reasonable output from s2nc:
```
s2nc localhost 8000 --ciphers test_all_rsa_kex
libcrypto: AWS-LC 1.49.1
CONNECTED:
Handshake: NEGOTIATED|FULL_HANDSHAKE|WITH_SESSION_TICKET
Client hello version: 33
Client protocol version: 33
Server protocol version: 33
Actual protocol version: 33
Server name: localhost
Curve: NONE
Cipher negotiated: AES128-SHA
Server signature negotiated: None+None <----HERE
Early Data status: NOT REQUESTED
Wire bytes in: 2704
Wire bytes out: 498
s2n is ready
Connected to localhost:8000
```
But on the s2nd side, we do report a signature:
```
s2nd localhost 8000 --ciphers test_all_rsa_kex
libcrypto: AWS-LC 1.49.1
Listening on localhost:8000
CONNECTED:
Handshake: NEGOTIATED|FULL_HANDSHAKE|WITH_SESSION_TICKET
Client hello version: 33
Client protocol version: 33
Server protocol version: 33
Actual protocol version: 33
Server name: localhost
Curve: NONE
Cipher negotiated: AES128-SHA
Server signature negotiated: RSA+SHA256 <----HERE
Early Data status: NOT REQUESTED
JA3: a24955ad4bc89eb0c960d34b2a6f1486
Wire bytes in: 498
Wire bytes out: 2704
s2n is ready
```

I'm guessing the problem is that the server always chooses a signature scheme as part of negotiating parameters. The client doesn't know what that scheme is because the server never actually send a signature.

### Need By Date:
None, no customer reach outs. I think this is just a visibility / logging / metrics issue.

### Solution:

We should make the server also report "None+None". Likely that means updating the signature algorithm selection logic to check for RSA kex.

* **Does this change what S2N sends over the wire?** If yes, explain.
* **Does this change any public APIs?** If yes, explain.
* **Which versions of TLS will this impact?**

### Requirements / Acceptance Criteria:

What must a solution address in order to solve the problem? How do we know the solution is complete?

* **RFC links:** Links to relevant RFC(s)
* **Related Issues:** Link any relevant issues
* **Will the Usage Guide or other documentation need to be updated?**
* **Testing:** How will this change be tested? Call out new integration tests, functional tests, or particularly interesting/important unit tests.
  * **Will this change trigger SAW changes?** Changes to the state machine, the s2n_handshake_io code that controls state transitions, the DRBG, or the corking/uncorking logic could trigger SAW failures.
  * **Should this change be fuzz tested?** Will it handle untrusted input? Create a separate issue to track the fuzzing work.

### Out of scope:

Is there anything the solution will intentionally NOT address?

[//]: #  (NOTE: If you believe this might be a security issue, please email aws-security@amazon.com instead of creating a GitHub issue. For more details, see the AWS Vulnerability Reporting Guide: https://aws.amazon.com/security/vulnerability-reporting/ )


</pr_description>

    66	/* Allocates and initializes memory for a new connection.
    67	 *
    68	 * Since customers can reuse a connection, ensure that values on the connection are
    69	 * initialized in `s2n_connection_wipe` where possible. */
    70	struct s2n_connection *s2n_connection_new(s2n_mode mode)
    71	{
    72	    struct s2n_blob blob = { 0 };
    73	    PTR_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_alloc(&blob, sizeof(struct s2n_connection)));
    74	    PTR_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_blob_zero(&blob));
    75	
    76	    /* Cast 'through' void to acknowledge that we are changing alignment,
    77	     * which is ok, as blob.data is always aligned.
    78	     */
    79	    struct s2n_connection *conn = (struct s2n_connection *) (void *) blob.data;
    80	
    81	    PTR_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_connection_set_config(conn, s2n_fetch_default_config()));
    82	
    83	    /* `mode` is initialized here since it's passed in as a parameter. */
    84	    conn->mode = mode;
    85	
    86	    /* Allocate the fixed-size stuffers */
    87	    blob = (struct s2n_blob){ 0 };
    88	    PTR_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_blob_init(&blob, conn->alert_in_data, S2N_ALERT_LENGTH));
    89	    PTR_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_stuffer_init(&conn->alert_in, &blob));
    90	
    91	    blob = (struct s2n_blob){ 0 };
    92	    PTR_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_blob_init(&blob, conn->ticket_ext_data, S2N_TLS12_TICKET_SIZE_IN_BYTES));
    93	    PTR_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_stuffer_init(&conn->client_ticket_to_decrypt, &blob));
    94	
    95	    /* Allocate long term hash and HMAC memory */
    96	    PTR_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_prf_new(conn));
    97	    PTR_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_handshake_hashes_new(&conn->handshake.hashes));
    98	
    99	    /* Initialize the growable stuffers. Zero length at first, but the resize
   100	     * in _wipe will fix that
   101	     */
   102	    blob = (struct s2n_blob){ 0 };
   103	    PTR_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_blob_init(&blob, conn->header_in_data, S2N_TLS_RECORD_HEADER_LENGTH));
   104	    PTR_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_stuffer_init(&conn->header_in, &blob));
   105	    PTR_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_stuffer_growable_alloc(&conn->out, 0));
   106	    PTR_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_stuffer_growable_alloc(&conn->buffer_in, 0));
   107	    PTR_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_stuffer_growable_alloc(&conn->handshake.io, 0));
   108	    PTR_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_timer_start(conn->config, &conn->write_timer));
   109	
   110	    /* NOTE: s2n_connection_wipe MUST be called last in this function.
   111	     *
   112	     * s2n_connection_wipe is used for initializing values but also used by customers to
   113	     * reset/reuse the connection. Calling it last ensures that s2n_connection_wipe is
   114	     * implemented correctly and safe.
   115	     */
   116	    PTR_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_connection_wipe(conn));
   117	    return conn;
   118	}
   119	
   120	static int s2n_connection_zero(struct s2n_connection *conn, int mode, struct s2n_config *config)
   121	{
   122	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   123	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(config);
   124	
   125	    /* Zero the whole connection structure */
   126	    POSIX_CHECKED_MEMSET(conn, 0, sizeof(struct s2n_connection));
   127	
   128	    conn->mode = mode;
   129	    conn->max_outgoing_fragment_length = S2N_DEFAULT_FRAGMENT_LENGTH;
   130	    conn->handshake.end_of_messages = APPLICATION_DATA;
   131	    s2n_connection_set_config(conn, config);
   132	
   133	    return 0;
   134	}
   135	
   136	S2N_RESULT s2n_connection_wipe_all_keyshares(struct s2n_connection *conn)
   137	{
   138	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   139	
   140	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_ecc_evp_params_free(&conn->kex_params.server_ecc_evp_params));
   141	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_ecc_evp_params_free(&conn->kex_params.client_ecc_evp_params));
   142	
   143	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_kem_group_free(&conn->kex_params.server_kem_group_params));
   144	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_kem_group_free(&conn->kex_params.client_kem_group_params));
   145	
   146	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   147	}
   148	
   149	static int s2n_connection_wipe_keys(struct s2n_connection *conn)
   150	{
   151	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   152	
   153	    /* Free any server key received (we may not have completed a
   154	     * handshake, so this may not have been free'd yet) */
   155	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_pkey_free(&conn->handshake_params.server_public_key));
   156	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_pkey_zero_init(&conn->handshake_params.server_public_key));
   157	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_pkey_free(&conn->handshake_params.client_public_key));
   158	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_pkey_zero_init(&conn->handshake_params.client_public_key));
   159	    s2n_x509_validator_wipe(&conn->x509_validator);
   160	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_dh_params_free(&conn->kex_params.server_dh_params));
   161	    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_connection_wipe_all_keyshares(conn));
   162	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_kem_free(&conn->kex_params.kem_params));
   163	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_free(&conn->handshake_params.client_cert_chain));
   164	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_free(&conn->ct_response));
   165	
   166	    return 0;
   167	}
   168	
   169	static int s2n_connection_free_managed_recv_io(struct s2n_connection *conn)
   170	{
   171	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   172	
   173	    if (conn->managed_recv_io) {
   174	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_free_object((uint8_t **) &conn->recv_io_context, sizeof(struct s2n_socket_read_io_context)));
   175	        conn->managed_recv_io = false;
   176	        conn->recv = NULL;
   177	    }
   178	    return S2N_SUCCESS;
   179	}
   180	
   181	static int s2n_connection_free_managed_send_io(struct s2n_connection *conn)
   182	{
   183	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   184	
   185	    if (conn->managed_send_io) {
   186	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_free_object((uint8_t **) &conn->send_io_context, sizeof(struct s2n_socket_write_io_context)));
   187	        conn->managed_send_io = false;
   188	        conn->send = NULL;
   189	    }
   190	    return S2N_SUCCESS;
   191	}
   192	
   193	static int s2n_connection_free_managed_io(struct s2n_connection *conn)
   194	{
   195	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_connection_free_managed_recv_io(conn));
   196	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_connection_free_managed_send_io(conn));
   197	    return S2N_SUCCESS;
   198	}
   199	
   200	static int s2n_connection_wipe_io(struct s2n_connection *conn)
   201	{
   202	    if (s2n_connection_is_managed_corked(conn) && conn->recv) {
   203	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_socket_read_restore(conn));
   204	    }
   205	    if (s2n_connection_is_managed_corked(conn) && conn->send) {
   206	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_socket_write_restore(conn));
   207	    }
   208	
   209	    /* Remove all I/O-related members */
   210	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_connection_free_managed_io(conn));
   211	
   212	    return 0;
   213	}
   214	
   215	static uint8_t s2n_default_verify_host(const char *host_name, size_t len, void *data)
   216	{
   217	    /* if present, match server_name of the connection using rules
   218	     * outlined in RFC6125 6.4. */
   219	
   220	    struct s2n_connection *conn = data;
   221	
   222	    if (conn->server_name[0] == '\0') {
   223	        return 0;
   224	    }
   225	
   226	    /* complete match */
   227	    if (strlen(conn->server_name) == len && strncasecmp(conn->server_name, host_name, len) == 0) {
   228	        return 1;
   229	    }
   230	
   231	    /* match 1 level of wildcard */
   232	    if (len > 2 && host_name[0] == '*' && host_name[1] == '.') {
   233	        const char *suffix = strchr(conn->server_name, '.');
   234	
   235	        if (suffix == NULL) {
   236	            return 0;
   237	        }
   238	
   239	        if (strlen(suffix) == len - 1 && strncasecmp(suffix, host_name + 1, len - 1) == 0) {
   240	            return 1;
   241	        }
   242	    }
   243	
   244	    return 0;
   245	}
   246	
   247	S2N_CLEANUP_RESULT s2n_connection_ptr_free(struct s2n_connection **conn)
   248	{
   249	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   250	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_connection_free(*conn));
   251	    *conn = NULL;
   252	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   253	}
   254	
   255	int s2n_connection_free(struct s2n_connection *conn)
   256	{
   257	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_connection_wipe_keys(conn));
   258	    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_psk_parameters_wipe(&conn->psk_params));
   259	
   260	    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_prf_free(conn));
   261	    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_handshake_hashes_free(&conn->handshake.hashes));
   262	
   263	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_connection_free_managed_io(conn));
   264	
   265	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_free(&conn->client_ticket));
   266	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_free(&conn->status_response));
   267	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_free(&conn->our_quic_transport_parameters));
   268	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_free(&conn->peer_quic_transport_parameters));
   269	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_free(&conn->server_early_data_context));
   270	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_free(&conn->tls13_ticket_fields.session_secret));
   271	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_free(&conn->buffer_in));
   272	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_free(&conn->in));
   273	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_free(&conn->out));
   274	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_free(&conn->handshake.io));
   275	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_free(&conn->post_handshake.in));
   276	    s2n_x509_validator_wipe(&conn->x509_validator);
   277	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_client_hello_free_raw_message(&conn->client_hello));
   278	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_free(&conn->application_protocols_overridden));
   279	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_free(&conn->cookie));
   280	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_free(&conn->cert_authorities));
   281	    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_crypto_parameters_free(&conn->initial));
   282	    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_crypto_parameters_free(&conn->secure));
   283	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_free_object((uint8_t **) &conn, sizeof(struct s2n_connection)));
   284	
   285	    return 0;
   286	}
   287	
   288	int s2n_connection_set_config(struct s2n_connection *conn, struct s2n_config *config)
   289	{
   290	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   291	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(config);
   292	
   293	    if (conn->config == config) {
   294	        return 0;
   295	    }
   296	
   297	    /* s2n_config invariant: any s2n_config is always in a state that respects the
   298	     * config->security_policy certificate preferences. Therefore we only need to
   299	     * validate certificates here if the connection is using a security policy override.
   300	     */
   301	    const struct s2n_security_policy *security_policy_override = conn->security_policy_override;
   302	    if (security_policy_override) {
   303	        POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_config_validate_loaded_certificates(config, security_policy_override));
   304	    }
   305	
   306	    /* We only support one client certificate */
   307	    if (s2n_config_get_num_default_certs(config) > 1 && conn->mode == S2N_CLIENT) {
   308	        POSIX_BAIL(S2N_ERR_TOO_MANY_CERTIFICATES);
   309	    }
   310	
   311	    s2n_x509_validator_wipe(&conn->x509_validator);
   312	
   313	    if (config->disable_x509_validation) {
   314	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_x509_validator_init_no_x509_validation(&conn->x509_validator));
   315	    } else {
   316	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_x509_validator_init(&conn->x509_validator, &config->trust_store, config->check_ocsp));
   317	        if (!conn->verify_host_fn_overridden) {
   318	            if (config->verify_host_fn != NULL) {
   319	                conn->verify_host_fn = config->verify_host_fn;
   320	                conn->data_for_verify_host = config->data_for_verify_host;
   321	            } else {
   322	                conn->verify_host_fn = s2n_default_verify_host;
   323	                conn->data_for_verify_host = conn;
   324	            }
   325	        }
   326	
   327	        if (config->max_verify_cert_chain_depth_set) {
   328	            POSIX_GUARD(s2n_x509_validator_set_max_chain_depth(&conn->x509_validator, config->max_verify_cert_chain_depth));
   329	        }
   330	    }
   331	    conn->tickets_to_send = config->initial_tickets_to_send;
   332	
   333	    if (conn->psk_params.psk_list.len == 0 && !conn->psk_mode_overridden) {
   334	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_connection_set_psk_mode(conn, config->psk_mode));
   335	        conn->psk_mode_overridden = false;
   336	    }
   337	
   338	    /* If at least one certificate does not have a private key configured,
   339	     * the config must provide an async pkey callback.
   340	     * The handshake could still fail if the callback doesn't offload the
   341	     * signature, but this at least catches configuration mistakes.
   342	     */
   343	    if (config->no_signing_key) {
   344	        POSIX_ENSURE(config->async_pkey_cb, S2N_ERR_NO_PRIVATE_KEY);
   345	    }
   346	
   347	    if (config->quic_enabled) {
   348	        /* If QUIC is ever enabled for a connection via the config,
   349	         * we should enforce that it can never be disabled by
   350	         * changing the config.
   351	         *
   352	         * Enabling QUIC indicates that the connection is being used by
   353	         * a QUIC implementation, which never changes. Disabling QUIC
   354	         * partially through a connection could also potentially be
   355	         * dangerous, as QUIC handles encryption.
   356	         */
   357	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_connection_enable_quic(conn));
   358	    }
   359	
   360	    if (config->send_buffer_size_override) {
   361	        conn->multirecord_send = true;
   362	    }
   363	
   364	    /* Historically, calling s2n_config_set_verification_ca_location enabled OCSP stapling
   365	     * regardless of the value set by an application calling s2n_config_set_status_request_type.
   366	     * We maintain this behavior for backwards compatibility.
   367	     *
   368	     * However, the s2n_config_set_verification_ca_location behavior predates client authentication
   369	     * support for OCSP stapling, so could only affect whether clients requested OCSP stapling. We
   370	     * therefore only have to maintain the legacy behavior for clients, not servers.
   371	     * 
   372	     * Note: The Rust bindings do not maintain the legacy behavior.
   373	     */
   374	    conn->request_ocsp_status = config->ocsp_status_requested_by_user;
   375	    if (config->ocsp_status_requested_by_s2n && conn->mode == S2N_CLIENT) {
   376	        conn->request_ocsp_status = true;
   377	    }
   378	
   379	    conn->config = config;
   380	    return S2N_SUCCESS;
   381	}
   382	
   383	int s2n_connection_server_name_extension_used(struct s2n_connection *conn)
   384	{
   385	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   386	    POSIX_ENSURE(conn->mode == S2N_SERVER, S2N_ERR_INVALID_STATE);
   387	    POSIX_ENSURE(!(conn->handshake.client_hello_received), S2N_ERR_INVALID_STATE);
   388	
   389	    conn->server_name_used = 1;
   390	    return S2N_SUCCESS;
   391	}

   405	
   406	int s2n_connection_release_buffers(struct s2n_connection *conn)
   407	{
   408	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   409	    POSIX_PRECONDITION(s2n_stuffer_validate(&conn->out));
   410	    POSIX_PRECONDITION(s2n_stuffer_validate(&conn->in));
   411	
   412	    POSIX_ENSURE(s2n_stuffer_is_consumed(&conn->out), S2N_ERR_STUFFER_HAS_UNPROCESSED_DATA);
   413	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_resize(&conn->out, 0));
   414	
   415	    POSIX_ENSURE(s2n_stuffer_is_consumed(&conn->in), S2N_ERR_STUFFER_HAS_UNPROCESSED_DATA);
   416	    if (s2n_stuffer_is_consumed(&conn->buffer_in)) {
   417	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_resize(&conn->buffer_in, 0));
   418	    }
   419	
   420	    POSIX_ENSURE(s2n_stuffer_is_consumed(&conn->post_handshake.in), S2N_ERR_STUFFER_HAS_UNPROCESSED_DATA);
   421	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_free(&conn->post_handshake.in));
   422	
   423	    POSIX_POSTCONDITION(s2n_stuffer_validate(&conn->out));
   424	    POSIX_POSTCONDITION(s2n_stuffer_validate(&conn->in));
   425	    return S2N_SUCCESS;
   426	}

    29	static S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_scheme_validate_for_send(struct s2n_connection *conn,
    30	        const struct s2n_signature_scheme *scheme)
    31	{
    32	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    33	
    34	    /* If no protocol has been negotiated yet, the actual_protocol_version will
    35	     * be equivalent to the client_protocol_version and represent the highest
    36	     * version supported.
    37	     */
    38	    RESULT_ENSURE_GTE(conn->actual_protocol_version, scheme->minimum_protocol_version);
    39	
    40	    /* QUIC only supports TLS1.3 */
    41	    if (s2n_connection_is_quic_enabled(conn) && scheme->maximum_protocol_version) {
    42	        RESULT_ENSURE_GTE(scheme->maximum_protocol_version, S2N_TLS13);
    43	    }
    44	
    45	    if (!s2n_is_rsa_pss_signing_supported()) {
    46	        RESULT_ENSURE_NE(scheme->sig_alg, S2N_SIGNATURE_RSA_PSS_RSAE);
    47	    }
    48	
    49	    if (!s2n_is_rsa_pss_certs_supported()) {
    50	        RESULT_ENSURE_NE(scheme->sig_alg, S2N_SIGNATURE_RSA_PSS_PSS);
    51	    }
    52	
    53	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
    54	}
    55	
    56	static bool s2n_signature_scheme_is_valid_for_send(struct s2n_connection *conn,
    57	        const struct s2n_signature_scheme *scheme)
    58	{
    59	    return s2n_result_is_ok(s2n_signature_scheme_validate_for_send(conn, scheme));
    60	}
    61	
    62	static S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_scheme_validate_for_recv(struct s2n_connection *conn,
    63	        const struct s2n_signature_scheme *scheme)
    64	{
    65	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(scheme);
    66	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    67	
    68	    RESULT_GUARD(s2n_signature_scheme_validate_for_send(conn, scheme));
    69	
    70	    if (scheme->maximum_protocol_version != S2N_UNKNOWN_PROTOCOL_VERSION) {
    71	        RESULT_ENSURE_LTE(conn->actual_protocol_version, scheme->maximum_protocol_version);
    72	    }
    73	
    74	    RESULT_ENSURE_NE(conn->actual_protocol_version, S2N_UNKNOWN_PROTOCOL_VERSION);
    75	    if (conn->actual_protocol_version >= S2N_TLS13) {
    76	        RESULT_ENSURE_NE(scheme->hash_alg, S2N_HASH_SHA1);
    77	        RESULT_ENSURE_NE(scheme->sig_alg, S2N_SIGNATURE_RSA);
    78	    }
    79	
    80	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
    81	}
    82	
    83	static bool s2n_signature_scheme_is_valid_for_recv(struct s2n_connection *conn,
    84	        const struct s2n_signature_scheme *scheme)
    85	{
    86	    return s2n_result_is_ok(s2n_signature_scheme_validate_for_recv(conn, scheme));
    87	}
    88	
    89	static S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_algorithms_get_legacy_default(struct s2n_connection *conn,
    90	        s2n_mode signer, const struct s2n_signature_scheme **default_sig_scheme)
    91	{
    92	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    93	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(default_sig_scheme);
    94	
    95	    s2n_authentication_method auth_method = 0;
    96	    if (signer == S2N_CLIENT) {
    97	        RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_get_auth_method_for_cert_type(
    98	                conn->handshake_params.client_cert_pkey_type, &auth_method));
    99	    } else {
   100	        RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure);
   101	        RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure->cipher_suite);
   102	        auth_method = conn->secure->cipher_suite->auth_method;
   103	    }
   104	
   105	    if (auth_method == S2N_AUTHENTICATION_ECDSA) {
   106	        *default_sig_scheme = &s2n_ecdsa_sha1;
   107	    } else {
   108	        *default_sig_scheme = &s2n_rsa_pkcs1_md5_sha1;
   109	    }
   110	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   111	}
   112	
   113	S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_algorithm_recv(struct s2n_connection *conn, struct s2n_stuffer *in)
   114	{
   115	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   116	
   117	    const struct s2n_signature_scheme **chosen_sig_scheme = NULL;
   118	    s2n_mode peer_mode = S2N_PEER_MODE(conn->mode);
   119	    if (peer_mode == S2N_CLIENT) {
   120	        chosen_sig_scheme = &conn->handshake_params.client_cert_sig_scheme;
   121	    } else {
   122	        chosen_sig_scheme = &conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme;
   123	    }
   124	
   125	    /* Before TLS1.2, signature algorithms were fixed instead of negotiated */
   126	    if (conn->actual_protocol_version < S2N_TLS12) {
   127	        return s2n_signature_algorithms_get_legacy_default(conn, peer_mode, chosen_sig_scheme);
   128	    }
   129	
   130	    uint16_t iana_value = 0;
   131	    RESULT_ENSURE(s2n_stuffer_read_uint16(in, &iana_value) == S2N_SUCCESS,
   132	            S2N_ERR_BAD_MESSAGE);
   133	
   134	    const struct s2n_signature_preferences *signature_preferences = NULL;
   135	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_connection_get_signature_preferences(conn, &signature_preferences));
   136	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(signature_preferences);
   137	
   138	    for (size_t i = 0; i < signature_preferences->count; i++) {
   139	        const struct s2n_signature_scheme *candidate = signature_preferences->signature_schemes[i];
   140	
   141	        if (candidate->iana_value != iana_value) {
   142	            continue;
   143	        }
   144	
   145	        if (!s2n_signature_scheme_is_valid_for_recv(conn, candidate)) {
   146	            continue;
   147	        }
   148	
   149	        *chosen_sig_scheme = candidate;
   150	        return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   151	    }
   152	
   153	    RESULT_BAIL(S2N_ERR_INVALID_SIGNATURE_SCHEME);
   154	}
   155	
   156	static S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_algorithms_validate_supported_by_peer(
   157	        struct s2n_connection *conn, uint16_t iana)
   158	{
   159	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   160	
   161	    const struct s2n_sig_scheme_list *peer_list = &conn->handshake_params.peer_sig_scheme_list;
   162	    for (size_t i = 0; i < peer_list->len; i++) {
   163	        if (peer_list->iana_list[i] == iana) {
   164	            return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   165	        }
   166	    }
   167	
   168	    RESULT_BAIL(S2N_ERR_NO_VALID_SIGNATURE_SCHEME);
   169	}
   170	
   171	static bool s2n_signature_algorithm_is_supported_by_peer(
   172	        struct s2n_connection *conn, uint16_t iana)
   173	{
   174	    return s2n_result_is_ok(s2n_signature_algorithms_validate_supported_by_peer(conn, iana));
   175	}
   176	
   177	S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_algorithm_select(struct s2n_connection *conn)
   178	{
   179	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   180	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure);
   181	    struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite = conn->secure->cipher_suite;
   182	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite);
   183	
   184	    const struct s2n_signature_scheme **chosen_sig_scheme = NULL;
   185	    if (conn->mode == S2N_CLIENT) {
   186	        chosen_sig_scheme = &conn->handshake_params.client_cert_sig_scheme;
   187	    } else {
   188	        chosen_sig_scheme = &conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme;
   189	    }
   190	
   191	    /* Before TLS1.2, signature algorithms were fixed instead of negotiated */
   192	    if (conn->actual_protocol_version < S2N_TLS12) {
   193	        RESULT_GUARD(s2n_signature_algorithms_get_legacy_default(conn, conn->mode, chosen_sig_scheme));
   194	        return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   195	    }
   196	
   197	    const struct s2n_signature_preferences *signature_preferences = NULL;
   198	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_connection_get_signature_preferences(conn, &signature_preferences));
   199	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(signature_preferences);
   200	
   201	    const struct s2n_signature_scheme *fallback_candidate = NULL;
   202	
   203	    /* We use local preference order, not peer preference order, so we iterate
   204	     * over the local preferences instead of over the options offered by the peer.
   205	     */
   206	    for (size_t i = 0; i < signature_preferences->count; i++) {
   207	        const struct s2n_signature_scheme *candidate = signature_preferences->signature_schemes[i];
   208	
   209	        /* Validates that a signature is valid to choose,
   210	         * including that it's allowed by the current protocol version.
   211	         */
   212	        if (!s2n_signature_scheme_is_valid_for_recv(conn, candidate)) {
   213	            continue;
   214	        }
   215	
   216	        if (s2n_is_sig_scheme_valid_for_auth(conn, candidate) != S2N_SUCCESS) {
   217	            continue;
   218	        }
   219	
   220	        /* s2n-tls first attempts to choose a signature algorithm offered by the peer.
   221	         * However, if that is not possible, we will attempt to continue the handshake
   222	         * anyway with an algorithm not offered by the peer. This fallback behavior
   223	         * is allowed by the RFC for TLS1.3 servers and partially allowed for TLS1.2
   224	         * servers that don't receive the signature_algorithms extension, but is
   225	         * otherwise an intentional deviation from the RFC.
   226	         *
   227	         * TLS1.3 servers:
   228	         *= https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8446#section-4.4.3
   229	         *# If the CertificateVerify message is sent by a server, the signature
   230	         *# algorithm MUST be one offered in the client's "signature_algorithms"
   231	         *# extension unless no valid certificate chain can be produced without
   232	         *# unsupported algorithms
   233	         *
   234	         * TLS1.3 clients:
   235	         *= https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8446#section-4.4.3
   236	         *= type=exception
   237	         *= reason=Compatibility with hypothetical faulty peers
   238	         *# If sent by a client, the signature algorithm used in the signature
   239	         *# MUST be one of those present in the supported_signature_algorithms
   240	         *# field of the "signature_algorithms" extension in the
   241	         *# CertificateRequest message.
   242	         *
   243	         * TLS1.2 servers:
   244	         *= https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5246#section-7.4.3
   245	         *= type=exception
   246	         *= reason=Compatibility with known faulty peers
   247	         *# If the client has offered the "signature_algorithms" extension, the
   248	         *# signature algorithm and hash algorithm MUST be a pair listed in that
   249	         *# extension.
   250	         *
   251	         * TLS1.2 clients:
   252	         *= https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5246#section-7.4.8
   253	         *= type=exception
   254	         *= reason=Compatibility with hypothetical faulty peers
   255	         *# The hash and signature algorithms used in the signature MUST be
   256	         *# one of those present in the supported_signature_algorithms field
   257	         *# of the CertificateRequest message.
   258	         */
   259	        bool is_peer_supported = s2n_signature_algorithm_is_supported_by_peer(
   260	                conn, candidate->iana_value);
   261	        if (is_peer_supported) {
   262	            *chosen_sig_scheme = candidate;
   263	            return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   264	        }
   265	
   266	        /**
   267	         *= https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5246#section-7.4.1.4.1
   268	         *# If the client does not send the signature_algorithms extension, the
   269	         *# server MUST do the following:
   270	         *#
   271	         *# -  If the negotiated key exchange algorithm is one of (RSA, DHE_RSA,
   272	         *#    DH_RSA, RSA_PSK, ECDH_RSA, ECDHE_RSA), behave as if client had
   273	         *#    sent the value {sha1,rsa}.
   274	         *#
   275	         *# -  If the negotiated key exchange algorithm is one of (DHE_DSS,
   276	         *#    DH_DSS), behave as if the client had sent the value {sha1,dsa}.
   277	         *#
   278	         *# -  If the negotiated key exchange algorithm is one of (ECDH_ECDSA,
   279	         *#    ECDHE_ECDSA), behave as if the client had sent value {sha1,ecdsa}.
   280	         *
   281	         * The default scheme for DSA is not used because s2n-tls does not support DSA certificates.
   282	         *
   283	         * These defaults are only relevant for TLS1.2, since TLS1.3 does not allow SHA1.
   284	         */
   285	        bool is_default = (candidate == &s2n_ecdsa_sha1 || candidate == &s2n_rsa_pkcs1_sha1);
   286	
   287	        /* If we ultimately cannot choose any algorithm offered by the peer,
   288	         * we will attempt negotiation with an algorithm not offered by the peer.
   289	         *
   290	         * The TLS1.2 RFC specifies default algorithms for use when no signature_algorithms
   291	         * extension is sent-- see the definition of is_default above.
   292	         *
   293	         * s2n-tls has encountered clients in the wild that support the TLS1.2
   294	         * default algorithms but do not include them in their signature_algorithms
   295	         * extension, likely due to a misreading of the RFC. So s2n-tls attempts
   296	         * to use the TLS1.2 defaults even when the client sends the signature_algorithms
   297	         * extension, and always treats them as the most preferred fallback option.
   298	         *
   299	         * If the TLS1.2 defaults are not possible-- for example, because TLS1.3
   300	         * or the security policy forbids SHA1-- we fallback to our own most
   301	         * preferred algorithm. In most cases a correctly implemented peer will reject
   302	         * this fallback, but the only alternative is to kill the connection here.
   303	         */
   304	        if (is_default) {
   305	            fallback_candidate = candidate;
   306	        } else if (fallback_candidate == NULL) {
   307	            fallback_candidate = candidate;
   308	        }
   309	    }
   310	
   311	    if (fallback_candidate) {
   312	        *chosen_sig_scheme = fallback_candidate;
   313	    } else {
   314	        RESULT_BAIL(S2N_ERR_NO_VALID_SIGNATURE_SCHEME);
   315	    }
   316	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   317	}
   318	
   319	S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_algorithms_supported_list_send(struct s2n_connection *conn, struct s2n_stuffer *out)
   320	{
   321	    const struct s2n_signature_preferences *signature_preferences = NULL;
   322	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_connection_get_signature_preferences(conn, &signature_preferences));
   323	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(signature_preferences);
   324	
   325	    struct s2n_stuffer_reservation size = { 0 };
   326	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_stuffer_reserve_uint16(out, &size));
   327	
   328	    for (size_t i = 0; i < signature_preferences->count; i++) {
   329	        const struct s2n_signature_scheme *const scheme = signature_preferences->signature_schemes[i];
   330	        RESULT_ENSURE_REF(scheme);
   331	        if (s2n_signature_scheme_is_valid_for_send(conn, scheme)) {
   332	            RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_stuffer_write_uint16(out, scheme->iana_value));
   333	        }
   334	    }
   335	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_stuffer_write_vector_size(&size));
   336	
   337	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   338	}
   339	
   340	int s2n_recv_supported_sig_scheme_list(struct s2n_stuffer *in, struct s2n_sig_scheme_list *sig_hash_algs)
   341	{
   342	    uint16_t length_of_all_pairs = 0;
   343	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_read_uint16(in, &length_of_all_pairs));
   344	    if (length_of_all_pairs > s2n_stuffer_data_available(in)) {
   345	        /* Malformed length, ignore the extension */
   346	        return 0;
   347	    }
   348	
   349	    if (length_of_all_pairs % 2) {
   350	        /* Pairs occur in two byte lengths. Malformed length, ignore the extension and skip ahead */
   351	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_skip_read(in, length_of_all_pairs));
   352	        return 0;
   353	    }
   354	
   355	    int pairs_available = length_of_all_pairs / 2;
   356	
   357	    if (pairs_available > TLS_SIGNATURE_SCHEME_LIST_MAX_LEN) {
   358	        POSIX_BAIL(S2N_ERR_TOO_MANY_SIGNATURE_SCHEMES);
   359	    }
   360	
   361	    sig_hash_algs->len = 0;
   362	
   363	    for (size_t i = 0; i < (size_t) pairs_available; i++) {
   364	        uint16_t sig_scheme = 0;
   365	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_read_uint16(in, &sig_scheme));
   366	
   367	        sig_hash_algs->iana_list[sig_hash_algs->len] = sig_scheme;
   368	        sig_hash_algs->len += 1;
   369	    }
   370	
   371	    return 0;
   372	}
   373	
   374	S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_algorithm_get_pkey_type(s2n_signature_algorithm sig_alg, s2n_pkey_type *pkey_type)
   375	{
   376	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(pkey_type);
   377	    *pkey_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_UNKNOWN;
   378	
   379	    switch (sig_alg) {
   380	        case S2N_SIGNATURE_RSA:
   381	        case S2N_SIGNATURE_RSA_PSS_RSAE:
   382	            *pkey_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA;
   383	            break;
   384	        case S2N_SIGNATURE_RSA_PSS_PSS:
   385	            *pkey_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA_PSS;
   386	            break;
   387	        case S2N_SIGNATURE_ECDSA:
   388	            *pkey_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_ECDSA;
   389	            break;
   390	        case S2N_SIGNATURE_MLDSA:
   391	            *pkey_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_MLDSA;
   392	            break;
   393	        default:
   394	            RESULT_BAIL(S2N_ERR_INVALID_SIGNATURE_ALGORITHM);
   395	    }
   396	
   397	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   398	}

    28	static S2N_RESULT s2n_check_tls13(const struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite,
    29	        struct s2n_connection *conn, bool *is_supported)
    30	{
    31	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(is_supported);
    32	    *is_supported = (s2n_connection_get_protocol_version(conn) >= S2N_TLS13);
    33	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
    34	}

    37	{
    38	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite);
    39	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    40	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(is_supported);
    41	
    42	    *is_supported = s2n_get_compatible_cert_chain_and_key(conn, S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA) != NULL;

    45	}

    47	static S2N_RESULT s2n_check_dhe(const struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite, struct s2n_connection *conn, bool *is_supported)
    48	{

    59	static S2N_RESULT s2n_check_ecdhe(const struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite, struct s2n_connection *conn, bool *is_supported)
    60	{

    70	static S2N_RESULT s2n_check_kem(const struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite, struct s2n_connection *conn, bool *is_supported)
    71	{
    72	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite);
    73	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    74	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(is_supported);
    75	
    76	    /* If any of the necessary conditions are not met, we will return early and indicate KEM is not supported. */
    77	    *is_supported = false;
    78	
    79	    const struct s2n_kem_preferences *kem_preferences = NULL;
    80	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_connection_get_kem_preferences(conn, &kem_preferences));
    81	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(kem_preferences);
    82	
    83	    if (!s2n_pq_is_enabled() || kem_preferences->kem_count == 0) {
    84	        return S2N_RESULT_OK;
    85	    }
    86	
    87	    const struct s2n_iana_to_kem *supported_params = NULL;
    88	    if (s2n_cipher_suite_to_kem(cipher_suite->iana_value, &supported_params) != S2N_SUCCESS) {
    89	        return S2N_RESULT_OK;
    90	    }
    91	
    92	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(supported_params);
    93	    if (supported_params->kem_count == 0) {
    94	        return S2N_RESULT_OK;
    95	    }
    96	
    97	    struct s2n_blob *client_kem_pref_list = &(conn->kex_params.client_pq_kem_extension);
    98	    const struct s2n_kem *chosen_kem = NULL;
    99	    if (client_kem_pref_list == NULL || client_kem_pref_list->data == NULL) {
   100	        /* If the client did not send a PQ KEM extension, then the server can pick its preferred parameter */
   101	        if (s2n_choose_kem_without_peer_pref_list(
   102	                    cipher_suite->iana_value, kem_preferences->kems, kem_preferences->kem_count, &chosen_kem)
   103	                != S2N_SUCCESS) {
   104	            return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   105	        }
   106	    } else {
   107	        /* If the client did send a PQ KEM extension, then the server must find a mutually supported parameter. */
   108	        if (s2n_choose_kem_with_peer_pref_list(
   109	                    cipher_suite->iana_value, client_kem_pref_list, kem_preferences->kems, kem_preferences->kem_count, &chosen_kem)
   110	                != S2N_SUCCESS) {
   111	            return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   112	        }
   113	    }
   114	
   115	    *is_supported = chosen_kem != NULL;
   116	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   117	}
   118	
   119	static S2N_RESULT s2n_configure_kem(const struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite, struct s2n_connection *conn)
   120	{
   121	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite);
   122	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   123	
   124	    RESULT_ENSURE(s2n_pq_is_enabled(), S2N_ERR_UNIMPLEMENTED);
   125	
   126	    const struct s2n_kem_preferences *kem_preferences = NULL;
   127	    RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_connection_get_kem_preferences(conn, &kem_preferences));
   128	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(kem_preferences);
   129	
   130	    struct s2n_blob *proposed_kems = &(conn->kex_params.client_pq_kem_extension);
   131	    const struct s2n_kem *chosen_kem = NULL;
   132	    if (proposed_kems == NULL || proposed_kems->data == NULL) {
   133	        /* If the client did not send a PQ KEM extension, then the server can pick its preferred parameter */
   134	        RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_choose_kem_without_peer_pref_list(cipher_suite->iana_value, kem_preferences->kems,
   135	                kem_preferences->kem_count, &chosen_kem));
   136	    } else {
   137	        /* If the client did send a PQ KEM extension, then the server must find a mutually supported parameter. */
   138	        RESULT_GUARD_POSIX(s2n_choose_kem_with_peer_pref_list(cipher_suite->iana_value, proposed_kems, kem_preferences->kems,
   139	                kem_preferences->kem_count, &chosen_kem));
   140	    }
   141	
   142	    conn->kex_params.kem_params.kem = chosen_kem;
   143	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   144	}
   145	
   146	static S2N_RESULT s2n_check_hybrid_ecdhe_kem(const struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite, struct s2n_connection *conn, bool *is_supported)
   147	{
   148	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite);
   149	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   150	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(is_supported);
   151	
   152	    bool ecdhe_supported = false;
   153	    bool kem_supported = false;
   154	    RESULT_GUARD(s2n_check_ecdhe(cipher_suite, conn, &ecdhe_supported));
   155	    RESULT_GUARD(s2n_check_kem(cipher_suite, conn, &kem_supported));
   156	
   157	    *is_supported = ecdhe_supported && kem_supported;
   158	
   159	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   160	}

   163	        struct s2n_connection *conn)
   164	{
   165	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   166	}

   168	static int s2n_kex_server_key_recv_read_data_unimplemented(struct s2n_connection *conn,
   169	        struct s2n_blob *data_to_verify, struct s2n_kex_raw_server_data *kex_data)
   170	{

   251	/* TLS1.3 key exchange is implemented differently from previous versions and does
   252	 * not currently require most of the functionality offered by s2n_kex.
   253	 * This structure primarily acts as a placeholder, so its methods are either
   254	 * noops or unimplemented.
   255	 */

   261	    .server_key_recv_parse_data = &s2n_kex_server_key_recv_parse_data_unimplemented,
   262	    .server_key_send = &s2n_kex_io_unimplemented,
   263	    .client_key_recv = &s2n_kex_io_unimplemented,
   264	    .client_key_send = &s2n_kex_io_unimplemented,
   265	    .prf = &s2n_kex_prf_unimplemented,
   266	};
   267	
   268	S2N_RESULT s2n_kex_supported(const struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite, struct s2n_connection *conn, bool *is_supported)
   269	{
   270	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite);
   271	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg);
   272	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg->connection_supported);
   273	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   274	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(is_supported);
   275	
   276	    RESULT_GUARD(cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg->connection_supported(cipher_suite, conn, is_supported));
   277	
   278	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   279	}
   280	
   281	S2N_RESULT s2n_configure_kex(const struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite, struct s2n_connection *conn)
   282	{
   283	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite);
   284	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg);
   285	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg->configure_connection);
   286	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
   287	
   288	    RESULT_GUARD(cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg->configure_connection(cipher_suite, conn));
   289	
   290	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   291	}
   292	
   293	S2N_RESULT s2n_kex_is_ephemeral(const struct s2n_kex *kex, bool *is_ephemeral)
   294	{
   295	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(kex);
   296	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(is_ephemeral);
   297	
   298	    *is_ephemeral = kex->is_ephemeral;
   299	
   300	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   301	}
   302	
   303	S2N_RESULT s2n_kex_server_key_recv_parse_data(const struct s2n_kex *kex, struct s2n_connection *conn, struct s2n_kex_raw_server_data *raw_server_data)
   304	{
   305	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(kex);

   312	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   313	}

   369	    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(premaster_secret);

   372	
   373	    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
   374	}
   375	
   376	bool s2n_kex_includes(const struct s2n_kex *kex, const struct s2n_kex *query)
   377	{
   378	    if (kex == query) {
   379	        return true;
   380	    }
   381	
   382	    if (kex == NULL || query == NULL) {
   383	        return false;
   384	    }
   385	
   386	    return query == kex->hybrid[0] || query == kex->hybrid[1];
   387	}

Now I understand the flow. When the server processes a client hello, it:
1. Chooses a cipher suite
2. If not PSK, calls `s2n_signature_algorithm_select(conn)` to select a signature scheme
3. Then selects certificates based on that

But for RSA kex, the server does NOT sign anything. The signature scheme is irrelevant. However, `s2n_signature_algorithm_select` still selects a scheme and stores it in `server_cert_sig_scheme`.

Let me check how the client side handles this. The client side function `s2n_signature_algorithm_recv` is called when the client receives a signature from the server. But for RSA kex, there's no ServerKeyExchange, so `s2n_signature_algorithm_recv` may not be called.

So `s2n_signature_algorithm_recv` is called from:

But the server calls `s2n_signature_algorithm_select` which sets `server_cert_sig_scheme` to a real scheme.

Now I understand the problem: the server should not select a signature scheme when the key exchange doesn't require one. The solution is to check if the chosen cipher suite uses RSA key exchange (which doesn't require a server signature) and skip setting the signature scheme (or set it to null).

2026-05-29 02:15:42,987 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I need to understand the approach. The PR description says:

> We should make the server also report "None+None". Likely that means updating the signature algorithm selection logic to check for RSA kex.

Looking at the `s2n_signature_algorithm_select` function (line 177 of `s2n_signature_algorithms.c`), it's called after the cipher suite has been chosen. So we can check if the chosen cipher suite uses RSA kex (or more generally, if the kex doesn't require a server signature), and if so, skip selecting a signature scheme (leave it as `s2n_null_sig_scheme`).

The key question: how to determine if the kex requires a signature? 

Looking at `s2n_rsa`:
- `is_ephemeral = false`
- `server_key_send = s2n_kex_io_unimplemented` (no server key exchange)

The server key exchange is what carries the signature. For RSA kex, there is no server key exchange. For DHE and ECDHE, there is a server key exchange with a signature.

So one approach: check if the kex method is RSA (non-ephemeral, no server key exchange).

But let me think more broadly. What about other kex methods that don't require a signature? 

Looking at the kex methods:
- `s2n_rsa`: non-ephemeral, no server key exchange -> no server signature
- `s2n_dhe`: ephemeral, has server key exchange -> needs server signature
- `s2n_ecdhe`: ephemeral, has server key exchange -> needs server signature
- `s2n_kem`: ephemeral, has server key exchange -> needs server signature
- `s2n_hybrid_ecdhe_kem`: ephemeral, has server key exchange -> needs server signature
- `s2n_tls13_kex`: ephemeral, but TLS 1.3 uses CertificateVerify instead

For TLS 1.3, the signature is sent in CertificateVerify, not ServerKeyExchange. So TLS 1.3 always needs a signature scheme.

So the simplest check is: if the kex is RSA (non-ephemeral, server_key_send is unimplemented), no server signature is needed.

But actually, the more general check would be: does the kex method have a `server_key_send` function that is implemented? If it's unimplemented, no server signature is needed.

Wait, but let me also check if there's already a function that checks this. Let me look at the handshake state machine to see how it decides whether to send ServerKeyExchange:

    40	/* clang-format off */
    41	struct s2n_handshake_action {
    42	    uint8_t record_type;
    43	    uint8_t message_type;
    44	    char writer;                /* 'S' or 'C' for server or client, 'B' for both */
    45	    int (*handler[2]) (struct s2n_connection * conn);
    46	};
    47	
    48	static int s2n_always_fail_send(struct s2n_connection *conn)
    49	{
    50	    /* This state should never be sending a handshake message. */
    51	    POSIX_BAIL(S2N_ERR_HANDSHAKE_UNREACHABLE);
    52	}
    53	
    54	static int s2n_always_fail_recv(struct s2n_connection *conn)
    55	{
    56	    /* This state should never have an incoming handshake message. */
    57	    POSIX_BAIL(S2N_ERR_HANDSHAKE_UNREACHABLE);
    58	}
    59

The `s2n_signature_algorithm_select` function handles both server and client modes:

```c
const struct s2n_signature_scheme **chosen_sig_scheme = NULL;
if (conn->mode == S2N_CLIENT) {
    chosen_sig_scheme = &conn->handshake_params.client_cert_sig_scheme;
} else {
    chosen_sig_scheme = &conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme;
}
```

For the client side, when called from `s2n_server_cert_request.c`, the client is selecting a signature scheme for client certificate verify. In that case, the client always needs a signature scheme (for client authentication), regardless of the kex method. So the RSA kex check should only apply to the server side.

Now let me think about the best approach:

Option 1: In `s2n_signature_algorithm_select`, after determining the mode is SERVER, check if the kex is ephemeral. If not ephemeral, set the signature scheme to `s2n_null_sig_scheme` and return.

Option 2: In the caller (`s2n_client_hello.c`), check if the kex requires a signature before calling `s2n_signature_algorithm_select`.

I think Option 1 is cleaner because it keeps the logic in the signature algorithm module.

But wait, I need to check if `s2n_signature_algorithm_select` is also called from TLS 1.3 paths. Let me check

2026-05-29 02:16:36,147 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
So `s2n_signature_algorithm_select` is called from two places:
1. `s2n_client_hello.c:622` - server processing client hello (server mode)
2. `s2n_server_cert_request.c:166` - client processing server cert request (client mode)

For the client mode, the client always needs a signature scheme for client certificate verify (if client auth is requested), regardless of kex. So the check should only be for server mode.

Now let me implement the fix. The approach: in `s2n_signature_algorithm_select`, when the connection mode is SERVER, check if the kex is ephemeral. If not ephemeral (RSA kex), leave the signature scheme as `s2n_null_sig_scheme` (which is already the default set during wipe) and return early.

Actually, looking more carefully at the code, `s2n_signature_algorithm_select` is also called for TLS 1.3 (through `s2n_client_hello.c:622`). In TLS 1.3, the kex is `s2n_tls13_kex` which has `is_ephemeral = true`, so the check would be fine.

But wait, for the server mode in `s2n_signature_algorithm_select`, there's another subtlety: the function also selects `client_cert_sig_scheme` when `conn->mode == S2N_CLIENT`. But for server mode, it selects `server_cert_sig_scheme`. The fix should only affect `server_cert_sig_scheme` when the server doesn't need to sign.

Let me write the fix now:







🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/tls/s2n_signature_algorithms.c   --old_str 'S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_algorithm_select(struct s2n_connection *conn)
{
    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure);
    struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite = conn->secure->cipher_suite;
    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite);

    const struct s2n_signature_scheme **chosen_sig_scheme = NULL;
    if (conn->mode == S2N_CLIENT) {
        chosen_sig_scheme = &conn->handshake_params.client_cert_sig_scheme;
    } else {
        chosen_sig_scheme = &conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme;
    }

    /* Before TLS1.2, signature algorithms were fixed instead of negotiated */
    if (conn->actual_protocol_version < S2N_TLS12) {
        RESULT_GUARD(s2n_signature_algorithms_get_legacy_default(conn, conn->mode, chosen_sig_scheme));
        return S2N_RESULT_OK;
    }' --new_str 'S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_algorithm_select(struct s2n_connection *conn)
{
    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure);
    struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite = conn->secure->cipher_suite;
    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite);

    const struct s2n_signature_scheme **chosen_sig_scheme = NULL;
    if (conn->mode == S2N_CLIENT) {
        chosen_sig_scheme = &conn->handshake_params.client_cert_sig_scheme;
    } else {
        chosen_sig_scheme = &conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme;
    }

    /* If the key exchange does not require a server signature,
     * keep the null signature scheme and return.
     *
     * With RSA key exchange, the server proves its ownership of the
     * RSA certificate by encrypting/decrypting the premaster secret
     * instead of performing a separate signature.
     */
    if (conn->mode == S2N_SERVER) {
        bool is_ephemeral = false;
        RESULT_GUARD(s2n_kex_is_ephemeral(cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg, &is_ephemeral));
        if (!is_ephemeral) {
            *chosen_sig_scheme = &s2n_null_sig_scheme;
            return S2N_RESULT_OK;
        }
    }

    /* Before TLS1.2, signature algorithms were fixed instead of negotiated */
    if (conn->actual_protocol_version < S2N_TLS12) {
        RESULT_GUARD(s2n_signature_algorithms_get_legacy_default(conn, conn->mode, chosen_sig_scheme));
        return S2N_RESULT_OK;
    }'

Actually, let me re-read the problem more carefully. The PR says:

> I'm guessing the problem is that the server always chooses a signature scheme as part of negotiating parameters. The client doesn't know what that scheme is because the server never actually send a signature.

So the server side reports a signature (e.g., RSA+SHA256) while the client reports None+None. The fix should make the server also report None+None.

But wait, I need to think about what exactly "Server signature negotiated" means from the API perspective. The functions `s2n_connection_get_selected_signature_algorithm` and `s2n_connection_get_selected_digest_algorithm` return the signature algorithm used for the server certificate. If RSA kex is used, the server doesn't actually sign anything, so it makes sense to return None/Anonymous.

But let me double-check by looking at how the client gets its "None+None" result. The client's `server_cert_sig_scheme` stays as `s2n_null_sig_scheme` because `s2n_signature_algorithm_recv` is never called for RSA kex (there's no ServerKeyExchange message). That's why the client reports None+None.

For the server, `s2n_signature_algorithm_select` is called and sets `server_cert_sig_scheme` to a real scheme. My fix makes the server skip selection if the kex is not ephemeral (RSA kex).

Now, let me verify that my change is correct by looking at edge cases:

1. **TLS 1.2 with RSA kex**: `is_ephemeral = false` → server sets null sig scheme. ✓

```c
S2N_RESULT s2n_kex_is_ephemeral(const struct s2n_kex *kex, bool *is_ephemeral)
{
    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(kex);
    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(is_ephemeral);
    *is_ephemeral = kex->is_ephemeral;
    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
}
```

   255	    struct s2n_blob data_to_sign = { 0 };
   256	
   257	    /* Call the negotiated key exchange method to send it's data */

   262	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_stuffer_write_uint16(out, sig_scheme->iana_value));
   263	    }
   264

   266	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_hash_init(signature_hash, sig_scheme->hash_alg));
   267	    POSIX_GUARD(s2n_hash_update(signature_hash, conn->handshake_params.client_random, S2N_TLS_RANDOM_DATA_LEN));

2026-05-29 02:21:19,293 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
So `s2n_server_key_send` uses `conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme` directly. If we set it to `s2n_null_sig_scheme`, and somehow `s2n_server_key_send` is called, it would fail because `s2n_null_sig_scheme` has `hash_alg = S2N_HASH_NONE` and `sig_alg = S2N_SIGNATURE_ANONYMOUS`. But for RSA kex, `s2n_server_key_send` is never called because the handshake state machine without `TLS12_PERFECT_FORWARD_SECRECY` doesn't include `SERVER_KEY`.

Let me verify this by looking at the state machine for `FULL_HANDSHAKE` (without PFS):

```
[NEGOTIATED | FULL_HANDSHAKE ] = {
    CLIENT_HELLO,
    SERVER_HELLO, SERVER_CERT, SERVER_HELLO_DONE,
    ...
}
```

There's no `SERVER_KEY`! So for RSA kex, the server never sends a ServerKeyExchange, and `s2n_server_key_send` is never called. Good.

Now let me also check that `s2n_signature_algorithm_select` is not used elsewhere for the server where it might need the signature scheme for something other than ServerKeyExchange. Looking at the usage:

1. `server_cert_sig_scheme` is used in `s2n_server_key_exchange.c` for both sending and receiving.
2. `server_cert_sig_scheme` is used in `s2n_tls13_certificate_verify.c` for TLS 1.3.
3. `server_cert_sig_scheme` is used in `s2n_auth_selection.c` for authentication selection.
4. `server_cert_sig_scheme` is returned by `s2n_connection_get_selected_signature_algorithm` and `s2n_connection_get_selected_digest_algorithm`.

For TLS 1.3, `is_ephemeral` is true, so we don't skip.

Wait! This is important. `s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth` at line 207 uses `server_cert_sig_scheme->sig_alg` to select the certificate. If we set `server_cert_sig_scheme` to `s2n_null_sig_scheme`, then `sig_alg` would be `S2N_SIGNATURE_ANONYMOUS`, and `s2n_signature_algorithm_get_pkey_type` would fail with `S2N_ERR_INVALID_SIGNATURE_ALGORITHM` because `S2N_SIGNATURE_ANONYMOUS` is not handled in the switch.

Let me check `s2n_signature_algorithm_get_pkey_type`:

```c
S2N_RESULT s2n_signature_algorithm_get_pkey_type(s2n_signature_algorithm sig_alg, s2n_pkey_type *pkey_type)
{
    RESULT_ENSURE_REF(pkey_type);
    *pkey_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_UNKNOWN;

    switch (sig_alg) {
        case S2N_SIGNATURE_RSA:
        case S2N_SIGNATURE_RSA_PSS_RSAE:
            *pkey_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA;
            break;
        case S2N_SIGNATURE_RSA_PSS_PSS:
            *pkey_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA_PSS;
            break;
        case S2N_SIGNATURE_ECDSA:
            *pkey_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_ECDSA;
            break;
        case S2N_SIGNATURE_MLDSA:
            *pkey_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_MLDSA;
            break;
        default:
            RESULT_BAIL(S2N_ERR_INVALID_SIGNATURE_ALGORITHM);
    }

    return S2N_RESULT_OK;
}
```

Indeed, `S2N_SIGNATURE_ANONYMOUS` would hit the default case and bail with an error. So my fix would break the certificate selection for RSA kex.

This means I need a different approach. Instead of setting the signature scheme to null before certificate selection, I should still allow the signature scheme to be selected (for certificate selection purposes) but then clear it after, or the API functions should check if a signature was actually performed.

Wait, let me re-read the PR description again:

> I'm guessing the problem is that the server always chooses a signature scheme as part of negotiating parameters. The client doesn't know what that scheme is because the server never actually send a signature.

> We should make the server also report "None+None". Likely that means updating the signature algorithm selection logic to check for RSA kex.

So the fix should be in the API functions `s2n_connection_get_selected_signature_algorithm` and `s2n_connection_get_selected_digest_algorithm`. They should check if the connection used RSA kex (non-ephemeral), and if so, return None/Anonymous instead of the selected signature scheme.

OR, we could modify `s2n_signature_algorithm_select` to not select a scheme for RSA kex, AND modify `s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth` to not rely on `server_cert_sig_scheme` for RSA kex.

But the latter is more invasive. Let me think about what makes more sense.

Actually, looking at `s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth`, it's called right after `s2n_signature_algorithm_select` in `s2n_client_hello.c`:

```c
/* And set the signature and hash algorithm used for key exchange signatures */
POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_algorithm_select(conn));

/* And finally, set the certs specified by the final auth + sig_alg combo. */
POSIX_GUARD(s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth(conn, &conn->handshake_params.our_chain_and_key));
```

So the certificate selection depends on the signature scheme. If we don't select a signature scheme, certificate selection would fail.

But for RSA kex, we still need to select a certificate - we just don't need to sign with it. The certificate is sent in the ServerCertificate message regardless of kex method. So the certificate selection needs to happen, but it shouldn't depend on a signature scheme for RSA kex.

Let me look at how `s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth` works:

```c
int s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth(struct s2n_connection *conn, struct s2n_cert_chain_and_key **chosen_certs)
{
    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme);
    s2n_signature_algorithm sig_alg = conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme->sig_alg;

    s2n_pkey_type cert_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_UNKNOWN;
    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_algorithm_get_pkey_type(sig_alg, &cert_type));

    *chosen_certs = s2n_get_compatible_cert_chain_and_key(conn, cert_type);
    S2N_ERROR_IF(*chosen_certs == NULL, S2N_ERR_CERT_TYPE_UNSUPPORTED);

    return S2N_SUCCESS;
}
```

It uses `sig_alg` to determine the `cert_type`, then gets a compatible cert. For RSA kex, we still need an RSA certificate. The auth method for the cipher suite is `S2N_AUTHENTICATION_RSA`, which corresponds to RSA certificates.

But wait, there's also `s2n_conn_find_name_matching_certs` called earlier (line 586) and `s2n_set_cipher_as_tls_server` (line 597) which already filter cipher suites based on available certificates. Let me trace through the certificate selection more carefully.

Actually, looking at `s2n_set_cipher_as_tls_server`, it likely checks auth_method compatibility. And `s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth` does the final selection. But for RSA kex, the auth_method is `S2N_AUTHENTICATION_RSA`, which means we need an RSA certificate. So we could modify `s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth` to use the cipher suite's auth method when the signature scheme is null/anonymous.

But this is getting complex. Let me reconsider.

Maybe the better approach is: keep the signature scheme selection as is (for internal purposes like certificate selection), but modify the public API functions (`s2n_connection_get_selected_signature_algorithm` and `s2n_connection_get_selected_digest_algorithm`) to check if the kex is non-ephemeral and return None.

Let me look at the API functions again:

```c
int s2n_connection_get_selected_signature_algorithm(struct s2n_connection *conn,
        s2n_tls_signature_algorithm *converted_scheme)
{
    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(converted_scheme);

    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_scheme_to_signature_algorithm(
            conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme, converted_scheme));

    return S2N_SUCCESS;
}
```

And `s2n_connection_get_selected_digest_algorithm`.

These are the functions used by the echo program to display the signature. If we modify these to check for RSA kex and return None, the server would also report "None+None".

But wait, there are also corresponding functions for client certificates: `s2n_connection_get_selected_client_cert_signature_algorithm` and `s2n_connection_get_selected_client_cert_digest_algorithm`. For client certificates, the signature is always needed (if client auth is requested), regardless of kex. So we should only modify the server-side functions.

But actually, for client certificates with RSA kex, the client still signs its CertificateVerify message. So the client cert signature scheme should be reported correctly.

Actually, looking at `s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth` again:

```c
int s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth(struct s2n_connection *conn, struct s2n_cert_chain_and_key **chosen_certs)
{
    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme);
    s2n_signature_algorithm sig_alg = conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme->sig_alg;

    s2n_pkey_type cert_type = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_UNKNOWN;
    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_algorithm_get_pkey_type(sig_alg, &cert_type));

    *chosen_certs = s2n_get_compatible_cert_chain_and_key(conn, cert_type);
    S2N_ERROR_IF(*chosen_certs == NULL, S2N_ERR_CERT_TYPE_UNSUPPORTED);

    return S2N_SUCCESS;
}
```

This function uses the signature scheme's sig_alg to determine the certificate type. For RSA kex, we need an RSA certificate. The auth_method for RSA kex cipher suites is `S2N_AUTHENTICATION_RSA`.

    40	 */
    41	
    42	int s2n_get_auth_method_for_cert_type(s2n_pkey_type cert_type, s2n_authentication_method *auth_method)
    43	{
    44	    switch (cert_type) {
    45	        case S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA:
    46	        case S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA_PSS:
    47	            *auth_method = S2N_AUTHENTICATION_RSA;
    48	            return S2N_SUCCESS;
    49	        case S2N_PKEY_TYPE_ECDSA:
    50	            *auth_method = S2N_AUTHENTICATION_ECDSA;
    51	            return S2N_SUCCESS;
    52	        case S2N_PKEY_TYPE_MLDSA:
    53	        case S2N_PKEY_TYPE_UNKNOWN:
    54	        case S2N_PKEY_TYPE_SENTINEL:
    55	            POSIX_BAIL(S2N_ERR_CERT_TYPE_UNSUPPORTED);
    56	    }
    57	    POSIX_BAIL(S2N_ERR_CERT_TYPE_UNSUPPORTED);
    58	}
    59	
    60	static int s2n_is_sig_alg_valid_for_cipher_suite(s2n_signature_algorithm sig_alg, struct s2n_cipher_suite *cipher_suite)
    61	{
    62	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(cipher_suite);
    63	
    64	    s2n_pkey_type cert_type_for_sig_alg = S2N_PKEY_TYPE_UNKNOWN;
    65	    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_algorithm_get_pkey_type(sig_alg, &cert_type_for_sig_alg));
    66	
    67	    /* Non-ephemeral key exchange methods require encryption, and RSA-PSS certificates
    68	     * do not support encryption.
    69	     *
    70	     * Therefore, if a cipher suite uses a non-ephemeral kex, then any signature
    71	     * algorithm that requires RSA-PSS certificates is not valid.
    72	     */
    73	    const struct s2n_kex *kex = cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg;
    74	    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(kex);
    75	    if (!kex->is_ephemeral) {
    76	        POSIX_ENSURE_NE(cert_type_for_sig_alg, S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA_PSS);
    77	    }
    78	
    79	    /* If a cipher suite includes an auth method, then the signature algorithm
    80	     * must match that auth method.
    81	     */
    82	    if (cipher_suite->auth_method != S2N_AUTHENTICATION_METHOD_SENTINEL) {
    83	        s2n_authentication_method auth_method_for_sig_alg;
    84	        POSIX_GUARD(s2n_get_auth_method_for_cert_type(cert_type_for_sig_alg, &auth_method_for_sig_alg));
    85	        POSIX_ENSURE_EQ(cipher_suite->auth_method, auth_method_for_sig_alg);
    86	    }
    87	
    88	    return S2N_SUCCESS;
    89	}
    90

The PR description says:
1. Problem: Server reports a signature scheme with RSA kex, but no signature is actually performed.
2. Solution: Make server also report "None+None".

My first approach (modifying `s2n_signature_algorithm_select`) was correct in spirit but broke certificate selection. However, I can fix `s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth` to handle the case where `server_cert_sig_scheme` is the null scheme.

Let me look at how `s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth` can determine the certificate type without relying on the signature scheme:

So `s2n_get_compatible_cert_chain_and_key` takes a `s2n_pkey_type`. For RSA kex, we need `S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA`.

Now let me reconsider my approach. Instead of modifying `s2n_signature_algorithm_select` and `s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth`, maybe I should just modify the API functions (`s2n_connection_get_selected_signature_algorithm` and `s2n_connection_get_selected_digest_algorithm`) to check for non-ephemeral kex and return None.

This approach is less invasive and directly addresses the reporting issue. The internal signature selection still works as before for certificate selection and other purposes. The API just reports "None+None" for RSA kex.

Let me implement this approach:









🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/tls/s2n_connection.c   --old_str 'int s2n_connection_get_selected_digest_algorithm(struct s2n_connection *conn,
        s2n_tls_hash_algorithm *converted_scheme)
{
    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(converted_scheme);

    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_scheme_to_tls_iana(
            conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme, converted_scheme));

    return S2N_SUCCESS;
}' --new_str 'int s2n_connection_get_selected_digest_algorithm(struct s2n_connection *conn,
        s2n_tls_hash_algorithm *converted_scheme)
{
    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
    POSIX_ENSURE_REF(converted_scheme);

    /* With RSA key exchange, the server proves its ownership of the
     * RSA certificate by encrypting/decrypting the premaster secret
     * instead of performing a separate signature. Therefore, no
     * signature algorithm is negotiated.
     */
    if (conn->mode == S2N_SERVER) {
        POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure);
        POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure->cipher_suite);
        const struct s2n_kex *kex = conn->secure->cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg;
        POSIX_ENSURE_REF(kex);
        bool is_ephemeral = false;
        POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_kex_is_ephemeral(kex, &is_ephemeral));
        if (!is_ephemeral) {
            *converted_scheme = S2N_TLS_HASH_NONE;
            return S2N_SUCCESS;
        }
    }

    POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_scheme_to_tls_iana(
            conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme, converted_scheme));

    return S2N_SUCCESS;
}'

1. **Server mode, RSA kex (non-ephemeral)**: Both functions should return None/Anonymous.
2. **Server mode, DHE/ECDHE kex (ephemeral)**: Both functions should return the actual selected scheme.
3. **Client mode, any kex**: Both functions should return the scheme received from the server (or null if none received).
4. **TLS 1.3**: `s2n_tls13_kex` is ephemeral, so server returns the selected scheme.

The API functions `s2n_connection_get_selected_signature_algorithm` and `s2n_connection_get_selected_digest_algorithm` are for the SERVER's signature. So they should always reflect the server's signature scheme, regardless of whether the caller is the client or server. 

But wait, if the client calls these functions, it should get the server's signature scheme. For RSA kex, the client already gets NONE because `server_cert_sig_scheme` is never set (remains null). So the check `conn->mode == S2N_SERVER` is actually redundant. The functions should just check if the kex is non-ephemeral regardless of mode. But to be safe, I'll keep the check to only affect the server's reporting. Actually, let me look at `s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth` more carefully. It's called right after `s2n_signature_algorithm_select`. If I modify `s2n_signature_algorithm_select` to skip selection for non-ephemeral kex (leaving `server_cert_sig_scheme` as null), then `s2n_select_certs_for_server_auth` would fail because it dereferences `server_cert_sig_scheme`.

- `S2N_AUTHENTICATION_RSA` maps to `S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA` (and `S2N_PKEY_TYPE_RSA_PSS`).

- Server mode, ephemeral kex: return the actual hash from `server_cert_sig_scheme`

Now, I'm thinking about whether my approach is the best one. Let me reconsider the PR description again:

> We should make the server also report "None+None". Likely that means updating the signature algorithm selection logic to check for RSA kex.

The PR says "updating the signature algorithm selection logic". My current approach modifies the API getter functions instead. But the API getter functions are what reports the signature scheme. The selection logic is internal and used for other purposes (certificate selection, etc.).

However, there's another consideration: what about the `s2n_connection_get_selected_client_cert_signature_algorithm` and `s2n_connection_get_selected_client_cert_digest_algorithm` functions? For client certificates, if RSA kex is used and client auth is requested, the client DOES sign its CertificateVerify message. So those should still report the actual signature scheme. My changes don't touch those.

Let me also think about whether the server might need to know the "real" signature scheme for any internal purpose after the handshake. Looking at the code, `server_cert_sig_scheme` is used in:
1. `s2n_server_key_exchange.c` - sending/receiving server key exchange
2. `s2n_tls13_certificate_verify.c` - TLS 1.3 cert verify
3. `s2n_auth_selection.c` - certificate selection
4. API getter functions

For RSA kex, items 1 and 2 are not applicable (no server key exchange, and TLS 1.3 always uses ephemeral kex). Item 3 happens during handshake setup. Item 4 is what we're fixing.

So my approach of modifying only the API getter functions is correct and minimal.

But wait, I should also consider: what if someone uses `s2n_connection_get_selected_signature_algorithm` on the server before the cipher suite is selected? My code accesses `conn->secure->cipher_suite` which may not be set yet. The function would fail. But this is probably acceptable because the signature scheme isn't meaningful until the cipher suite is selected.

Also, I added `POSIX_ENSURE_REF` checks for `conn->secure`, `conn->secure->cipher_suite`, and `kex`. If any of these are NULL, the function returns an error. This is a change from the previous behavior which would have succeeded (returning whatever was in `server_cert_sig_scheme`). But this should be fine because these functions are meant to be called after the handshake is complete.

Let me now think about whether I should also update `s2n_connection_get_selected_client_cert_signature_algorithm` and `s2n_connection_get_selected_client_cert_digest_algorithm`. Looking at the PR description, it only mentions the server signature. The client certificate functions should continue to report the actual scheme because the client does sign its CertificateVerify message even with RSA kex.

But wait, for the client side: if the server doesn't request client authentication, then `client_cert_sig_scheme` remains null, and the functions would return None. That's already correct.

5. `s2n_signature_algorithms.c:122,188` - setting the scheme during selection/recv
6. `s2n_server_key_exchange.c:52,252` - server key exchange (ephemeral kex only)

I notice that the tests at lines 245-246 and 296-297 create a `S2N_CLIENT` connection and expect `S2N_TLS_HASH_NONE` / `S2N_TLS_SIGNATURE_ANONYMOUS`. With my change, when the connection is a client, it skips the non-ephemeral check (because `conn->mode == S2N_CLIENT`), so it goes to the normal path and returns the null scheme. That's fine.

But wait, what about a server connection? The test creates a `S2N_CLIENT` connection, so my check `conn->mode == S2N_SERVER` would be false, and it proceeds normally. The test should still pass.

However, at lines 258-276, the test sets `server_cert_sig_scheme` to various test schemes and expects specific outputs. This test uses a `S2N_CLIENT` connection, so my server-only check wouldn't interfere. Good.

Now I'm thinking: should I also add a similar check for the case where the connection mode is SERVER in these test scenarios? The tests would need to set up a proper cipher suite with a non-ephemeral kex to trigger my new code path. But since the user said they already took care of test changes, I won't worry about that.

Let me now think about potential edge cases I might have missed:

1. **What if `conn->secure` is NULL?** My code checks `POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure)` which returns an error. But the previous code didn't require `conn->secure`. This could break callers that call these functions before the handshake completes. However, the functions are documented as returning the "selected" signature algorithm, which only makes sense after the handshake. So this should be fine.

2. **What if `conn->secure->cipher_suite` is NULL?** Same as above.

3. **What if `conn->secure->cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg` is NULL?** Same as above.

4. **What about TLS 1.3 with mutual auth?** The server still signs its CertificateVerify (TLS 1.3 always uses ephemeral kex), so `is_ephemeral` is true and the actual scheme is returned. Client auth also works because we don't modify the client cert functions.

+    /* With RSA key exchange, the server proves its ownership of the
+     * RSA certificate by encrypting/decrypting the premaster secret
+     * instead of performing a separate signature. Therefore, no
+     * signature algorithm is negotiated.
+     */
+    if (conn->mode == S2N_SERVER) {
+        POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure);
+        POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure->cipher_suite);
+        const struct s2n_kex *kex = conn->secure->cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg;
+        POSIX_ENSURE_REF(kex);
+        bool is_ephemeral = false;
+        POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_kex_is_ephemeral(kex, &is_ephemeral));
+        if (!is_ephemeral) {
+            *converted_scheme = S2N_TLS_HASH_NONE;
+            return S2N_SUCCESS;
+        }
+    }
+
     POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_signature_scheme_to_tls_iana(
             conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme, converted_scheme));
 
@@ -1693,6 +1712,24 @@ int s2n_connection_get_selected_signature_algorithm(struct s2n_connection *conn,
     POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn);
     POSIX_ENSURE_REF(converted_scheme);
 
+    /* With RSA key exchange, the server proves its ownership of the
+     * RSA certificate by encrypting/decrypting the premaster secret
+     * instead of performing a separate signature. Therefore, no
+     * signature algorithm is negotiated.
+     */
+    if (conn->mode == S2N_SERVER) {
+        POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure);
+        POSIX_ENSURE_REF(conn->secure->cipher_suite);
+        const struct s2n_kex *kex = conn->secure->cipher_suite->key_exchange_alg;
+        POSIX_ENSURE_REF(kex);
+        bool is_ephemeral = false;
+        POSIX_GUARD_RESULT(s2n_kex_is_ephemeral(kex, &is_ephemeral));
+        if (!is_ephemeral) {
+            *converted_scheme = S2N_TLS_SIGNATURE_ANONYMOUS;
+            return S2N_SUCCESS;
+        }
+    }
+

             conn->handshake_params.server_cert_sig_scheme, converted_scheme));
